Olivetti wins a bitterly fought takeover battle for control of rival Telecom Italia, confirming the advent of
U.S.-style capitalism in Europe and portending a reshuffling of the continent's telecom alliances. Olivetti, an
upstart telecom concern, will spend almost $33 billion to purchase its stake, which it plans to finance in part
by issuing $7.9 billion in bonds.
25
Cendant announces plans to sell its vehicle-leasing unit to Avis for $1.8 billion in an effort to focus its
operations on travel, real estate and direct marketing. Cendant also plans to sell other businesses to raise up
to $1.5 billion.
Conrail's breakup is raising hopes for a boost in industrial development and railroad shipping in the Northeast.
The $10 billion acquisition and carve-up by Norfolk Southern and CSX end Conrail's rail-freight monopoly.
A House report lists a devastating array of Chinese arms-technology thefts. The espionage inquiry finds that
Beijing has stolen U.S. design data for nearly all elements needed for a major nuclear attack on the U.S.,
such as advanced warheads, missiles and guidance systems.
26
Charter Communications plans to buy Falcon Cable TV for about $2 billion in cash and stock, and the
assumption of another $1.6 billion in debt. A day later, Charter says it plans to buy Fanch Communications in
a deal valued at just over $2 billion, which would make it the nation's fourth-biggest cable-TV company.
28
CBS's Infinity Broadcasting unit agrees to buy Outdoor Systems, a billboard company, for $6.5 billion in stock,
making Infinity the No. 1 U.S. outdoor-ad firm.
Nasdaq's parent approves a push for extended trading hours. But the NASD pulls back from setting a
timetable and calls for the move to be coordinated with the Big Board.
Exxon and Mobil shareholders overwhelmingly approve an $81.2 billion combination, which will create the
world's largest oil company.
A Dutch court upholds Pinault Printemps Redoute's pact to acquire a 42% stake in Gucci, bringing to an end
a bitter takeover battle with LVMH over the luxury group.
JUNE
1
AmSouth agrees to buy First American in a $6.3 billion stock-for-stock deal, say people familiar with the
matter. The move would create a strong Southeastern banking franchise with $40 billion in assets.
MCI WorldCom is buying SkyTel for $1.3 billion in stock and assuming $525 million in debt. The deal gives
MCI a nationwide two-way wireless messaging network, but MCI still lacks a major cellular-telephone
presence.
2
Merrill Lynch's plan to offer low-cost online trading faces hurdles, as the brokerage firm attempts to build a
large discount-trading operation by Dec. 1.
Liberty Media plans to acquire Associated Group, the largest investor in Teligent, in a stock deal valued at
about $2.8 billion, plus debt assumption. The move gives Liberty its first exposure in the world of
fixed-wireless communications.
3

--- Page 263 ---
Page 263 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
Roche will allow Genentech to remain an independent, publicly traded company. Roche will buy the
remaining 33% of the biotechnology firm's stock that it doesn't already own for about $4 billion and then
reissue between 10% and 19% of Genentech's stock.
Texaco ends merger talks with its West Coast rival Chevron, calling the price and terms "unacceptable."
4
South Africa's African National Congress wins a huge victory in elections. President-elect Thabo Mbeki,
elected South Africa's second black president, will succeed Nelson Mandela.
The Big Board says it won't open for evening trading for at least another year, stepping back from previous
statements that it could start as early as next month.
7
Allied Signal agrees to buy Honeywell for $13.8 billion in stock, creating an aerospace parts-and-electronics
powerhouse, say people familiar with the situation.
8
Indonesians vote amid relative peace and a 90% turnout in the first parliamentary elections since Suharto's
ouster. A coalition led by Megawati Sukarnoputri is favored to secure a plurality.
Goldman Sachs, Merrill Lynch and Madoff Securities are teaming up to create a new electronic trading
system that they hope will rival the Big Board.
9
GMAC agrees to buy a commercial-finance unit of Bank of New York for $1.8 billion. The purchase continues
the GM unit's search for growth outside its auto-lending business.
10
Former slave workers of the Nazis would be compensated according to the cost of living in countries where
they now reside, according to a plan that big German firms are to present today. The fund's size hasn't been
set, but talks participants say it will be at least $1 billion.
11
Ralston Purina says it will spin off to shareholders its struggling Energizer battery business and focus on the
company's growing pet-food business. Energizer, which is being squeezed by rivals Duracell and Rayovac,
could have a stand-alone market capitalization of between $2.3 billion and $4.8 billion, analysts say.
Coke's bottler in Belgium recalls 2.5 million bottles of Coke after schoolchildren there become ill. Coke's
bottle and can products are banned from sale by the Belgian government for an indefinite period after more
illnesses are reported. Reports of illnesses spread to France.
NATO halts its bombing as Serb forces start their pullout from Kosovo. Events moved rapidly following an
agreement earlier in the week on a withdrawal plan.
14
Qwest enters a $55 billion bid in cash and stock to buy U S West and Frontier. The hostile offers top Global
Crossing's previous stock offers, now more than $42 billion, to merge with the two firms in separate deals.
Qwest's move, which assumes $11.4 billion in debt, sets up a bidding war between two rivals that are
positioned as carriers of Internet traffic.
15
Wal-Mart makes a cash offer to acquire British supermarket chain Asda for about $10.8 billion, outbidding
British retailer Kingfisher. The deal will give Wal-Mart a strong presence in Europe and meet its longtime goal
of doubling its international operations.
The Bank of Japan intervenes in currency markets to halt a rise in the yen, spending between $5 billion and
$10 billion, currency traders say.
17

--- Page 264 ---
Page 264 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
New documents in Microsoft's antitrust trial show that the company kept an "enemies list" of small software
makers and that Bill Gates discussed how to leak an e-mail to the press.
21
Connecticut money manager Martin Frankel may have played a central role in the disappearance of hundreds
of millions of dollars from up to eight insurers, which are now in receivership, the FBI and insurance
regulators allege.
22
Abbott Laboratories agrees to acquire Alza for $7.3 billion in stock, bolstering the medical-products giant's
growth prospects.
AOL says it will invest $1.5 billion in Hughes Electronics to promote satellite delivery of Internet services, in a
vote of confidence in satellites as a consumer high-capacity technology.
23
General Dynamics plans to purchase three of GTE's military-communications units for $1.05 billion. The
move is intended to boost the contractor's operations in some of the Pentagon's fastest-growing segments.
24
American Airlines is under examination by federal safety officials for a series of accidents over the past six
years, including a recent one in Arkansas, that all seem to involve pilot miscues.
Lloyds TSB confirms plans to acquire Scottish Widows in an $11.13 billion deal that will create the U.K.'s
second-largest provider of life insurance, pensions and mutual funds.
VoiceStream Wireless agrees to buy Omnipoint in a deal valued at $2.04 billion, furthering the wave of
consolidations in the U.S. wireless industry.
NiSource is expected to launch a hostile $68-a-share tender offer for Columbia Energy, after Columbia's
board rejected its $5.7 billion unsolicited bid.
28
Suez Lyonnaise des Eaux is set to announce that it is launching a $4.1 billion tender offer for Illinois-based
Nalco Chemical, according to people familiar with the transaction. The deal would make the French utility a
world leader in water-treatment services.
30
CMGI agrees to buy an 83% stake in AltaVista, an Internet search
engine, from Compaq for $2.3 billion. The stock deal will give Compaq a
16.4% stake in CMGI, making Compaq the company's largest outside
investor.
JULY
1
The Fed lifts its key interest rate by one-fourth of a percentage point but thrills financial markets by
suggesting it might not raise rates again in the "near term."
7
Hillary Clinton gears up for a campaign for a Senate seat from New York.
8
Tobacco firms are found liable for causing lung cancer, heart disease and other illnesses by a state court jury
in Miami, in the first class-action lawsuit on behalf of injured smokers to go to trial. The verdict could expose
the nation's top five cigarette makers to billions in damages.
Cox Communications agrees to swap its AT&T stock for cable-TV systems in the South and West in a deal
valued at $2.8 billion, part of AT&T's reshaping of its cable empire.
12

--- Page 265 ---
Page 265 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
DuPont lays out plans for a final split from its Conoco unit, offering to swap $11.65 billion in Conoco stock for
13% of DuPont's shares outstanding.
13
Schlumberger will combine its offshore contract-drilling operations with Transocean Offshore in a $3.26 billion
stock deal, creating the world's largest offshore-energy drilling company.
14
Britain's BOC accepts an $11.17 billion takeover bid from France's Air Liquide and U.S.-based Air Products.
15
Apple's quarterly profit doubles to $203 million, again beating Wall Street's bullish forecasts, as its popular
iMac shows little sign of fading.
19
Qwest wins US West for $35 billion after it withdraws its offer for Frontier, ending a monthlong takeover battle
between Qwest and Global Crossing. A complex compromise was brokered after Global Crossing told US
West it wouldn't raise its original $30 billion offer to match Qwest's latest bid. Global Crossing will proceed
with its $11.1 billion Frontier merger.
France's Elf Aquitaine will launch a $50.97 billion cash-and-stock counterbid to buy TotalFina, which on July 5
unveiled a hostile $42.81 billion bid for Elf, its domestic oil-industry rival. A combination would create France's
largest company in terms of stock-market capitalization and the world's fourth-largest oil concern based on
capitalization and output.
19
John F. Kennedy Jr.'s plane, with his wife, Carolyn, and her sister Lauren Bessette also aboard, is the object
of a massive search. The 38-year-old Kennedy was piloting a Piper Saratoga when it left New Jersey. The
plane and bodies are later discovered after an intense search by the Coast Guard, and the ashes are cast
into the sea in a private ceremony.
21
Johnson & Johnson is near an agreement to buy Centocor in a stock deal valued at about $4.9 billion, people
familiar with the situation say.
Punch Taverns wins the takeover battle for Allied Domecq's pub unit in a $4.35 billion deal, making Punch
Britain's second-biggest pub operator. Allied Domecq had agreed to sell the unit to Whitbread for $3.84
billion, but Punch raised its bid to derail the offer.
22
UPS plans to sell 10% of its shares in what is likely to be one of the biggest IPOs ever. Analysts and people
familiar with UPS's plans say the sale should generate at least $3 billion, enabling UPS to use stock for
acquisitions.
23
The House votes 379-45 for a $268.6 billion Pentagon bill that cuts F-22 funds, throwing a potential monkey
wrench into Lockheed Martin's financial-recovery strategy.
Microsoft is making plans for an industry no longer dominated by the PC. Its new vision statement was
broadened to include Web-based software and services and other devices.
26
The U.S. and Vietnam reach a landmark trade accord after Hanoi signaled a willingness to embrace
Western-style economic reforms.
The Big Board is contemplating a stock offering within four months. As a public company, the exchange
would be able to better compete with the new electronic-trading systems.
Cable & Wireless is nearing a pact to sell the residential cable operations of its unit to cable firm NTL for
about $12.7 billion in cash and stock, people familiar with the situation say.

--- Page 266 ---
Page 266 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
27
Venezuelans vote for a 131-seat assembly that President Chavez wants to rewrite the constitution and close
the Congress and the Supreme Court. Chavez wins a big victory in the elections, with his candidates taking
90% of the seats. Opposition politicians pledge to fight any bid to abolish democratic institutions.
Cox Communications plans to acquire the cable-television assets of Gannett for $2.7 billion, further
consolidating the cable-TV business.
28
Britain's Reckitt & Colman agrees to merge with Benckiser in a $3.5 billion stock deal. The combined entity
would be the world's largest manufacturer of household-cleaning products, excluding laundry detergents.
British Telecommunications will buy the 40% it doesn't own in mobile-phone operator Cellnet for $5 billion.
29
A $4.5 billion Russia loan is approved by the IMF, which, in effect, rolled over loans suspended after
Moscow's devaluation last year.
Compaq posts a $184 million quarterly loss and says it will take a $700 million to $900 million restructuring
charge in the third period. The charge will cover plant closings and the cutting of as many as 8,000 positions.
Charter Communications plans to offer $3.45 billion of shares in an IPO, tapping into demand for Internet and
cable stocks.
A gunman kills at least nine in Atlanta, allegedly angry over recent day-trading losses. Mark O. Barton, a
44-year-old day trader, killed himself after a five-hour manhunt. Shootings occurred at two Buckhead district
buildings housing All-Tech Investment Group and a second firm serving day traders.
Indonesia's Megawati claims her allies' victory in June parliamentary elections entitled her to the presidency,
and calls on Habibie to step aside. The president is supposed to be named by a special assembly meeting in
the fall.
30
Martha Stewart plans an IPO to sell as much as $100 million of stock and use part of the proceeds to buy
back most of Time Warner's stake.
AUGUST
2
Fidelity National Financial will buy larger rival Chicago Title for $1.2 billion in cash and stock, creating the
nation's biggest title-insurance firm.
A Holocaust panel is recommending that five big European insurers should pay victims of the Nazis or their
families about 10 times the face value of policies from the era. That would put a settlement in the
multibillion-dollar range.
4
British American Tobacco agrees to purchase the 58% of Canada's Imasco it doesn't own for $6.8 billion and
sell Imasco's financial-services unit to Toronto-Dominion for $5.2 billion.
5
Dow Chemical agrees to buy rival Union Carbide for $8.89 billion in stock. The transaction, due to close early
next year, would create a firm with about $24 billion in annual sales, roughly equal to that of DuPont, the
largest U.S. chemical maker. Carbide shares rise 22% on the news.
6
Congress passes big GOP tax cuts, setting up a sharp political confrontation. The $792 billion package goes
to Clinton for a promised veto next month.
Swissair offers to accept liability, along with Boeing and Delta, for the crash off Nova Scotia last year if
plaintiffs in suits against the firms agree to waive punitive-damages claims. Swissair is facing claims totaling
$16 billion in the crash that killed 229 people.

--- Page 267 ---
Page 267 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
9
MCI WorldCom plans to cut long-distance rates during off-peak hours to as low as five cents a minute, paving
the way for another wave of price cuts in the consumer long-distance market. AT&T responds later in the
month with a seven-cents-a-minute, 24-hour-a-day plan.
Deutsche Telekom agrees to buy British wireless operator One2One for $11.12 billion in a deal that is crucial
to its international ambitions. One2One is owned by Cable & Wireless and MediaOne.
Volvo agrees to buy rival Swedish truck manufacturer Scania for $7.53 billion, a deal that will join the world's
No. 2 and No. 3 heavy-truck makers.
10
Three aluminum companies are in talks to form the world's biggest producer of the metal. Alcan of Canada,
Pechiney of France and Alusuisse Lonza of Switzerland would attempt to build a rival to U.S. aluminum giant
Alcoa, people familiar with the situation say. The $10.6 billion deal would also form a leading packaging
concern with more than $20 billion in revenue.
12
Alcoa discloses an unsolicited $4.1 billion takeover bid for rival Reynolds, responding swiftly to the merger
announced by Alcan, Pechiney and Alusuisse Lonza. Reynolds's board rejects the offer. Alcoa responds by
launching a full-blown hostile bid for Reynolds, starting a cash tender offer of $65 a share, or $4.1 billion, and
initiating a process to oust Reynolds's board. A week later, Reynolds agrees to be acquired by Alcoa for
$4.35 billion. The deal unites the world's largest aluminum maker with the third-largest.
16
Iridium files for Chapter 11 bankruptcy-law protection from creditors. The Motorola-backed concern's move is
the latest in a series of stumbles in the fledgling satellite-communications industry.
French bank Banque Nationale de Paris wins control of Paribas with a $20.3 billion offer. But BNP's $18.8
billion takeover bid for Societe Generale fails to win a majority of shares, foiling its three-way merger attempt
and hopes of creating a $1 trillion European bank.
17
A 7.4 earthquake strikes western Turkey. In following weeks, the official death toll passes 14,000. Turkey's
parliament passes $20 billion in new taxes to help pay for damage.
VNU plans to buy TV-ratings service Nielsen for $2.5 billion. The Dutch concern would gain one of the most
high-profile names in U.S. media.
18
Coca-Cola Beverages says merger talks with another European bottler, Hellenic Bottling, first announced in
June, are close to producing an agreement that would create the second-biggest Coke bottler. The stock
swap would value CCB, a British bottler, at around $3 billion.
19
Food Lion sets a pact to buy grocer Hannaford Brothers, as grocery-sector consolidation continues its rapid
pace. The cash and stock deal is designed to give Hannaford stockholders $3.33 billion.
20
The world's largest bank would be formed by three of Japan's biggest banks, which are planning to unite in a
holding company, an official at one of the concerns says. Fuji, Dai-Ichi Kangyo and Industrial Bank of Japan
would unite in the fall of 2000 and have $1.26 trillion in assets.
The U.S. trade deficit rises to $24.62 billion in June, setting a record.
Veba and Viag are in talks to merge the big German utility companies in a deal that could be valued at
roughly $15 billion, according to people familiar with the situation.
23

--- Page 268 ---
Page 268 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
Law-enforcement authorities, alerted to the suspected laundering of billions of dollars linked to Russian
organized crime, investigate whether Bank of New York was one of a chain of banks that were conduits for
about $200 million that may have been diverted from loans to Russia made by the IMF.
The Chicago Stock Exchange plans to offer an extra two-hour floor-trading session in the evening, the first
U.S. exchange to make such a move.
Comsat shareholders approve the satellite concern's $2.2 billion
acquisition by Lockheed. But the aerospace and defense company faces
obstacles, including negotiating a deal to sell its 14% stake in Comsat
rival Loral.
24
Suez Lyonnaise moves to buy out its U.S. municipal-water affiliate, United Water, in a $1 billion deal that
strengthens the French company's position as the world's leading water-services provider and caps a U.S.
shopping spree.
25
World Bank aid to Indonesia will stop if Jakarta doesn't swiftly get to the bottom of allegations that funds were
siphoned from a nationalized bank to a firm tied to the ruling party, the agency says. About $1 billion in loans
are pending.
The Fed raises two key interest rates a notch in a pre-emptive strike against inflation, but suggests the
moves could well be the last for the foreseeable future. The increase in the federal funds target rate to 5.25%
from 5% was widely expected, and investor reaction was muted.
Late trading in some stocks from the Big Board and Nasdaq is set to begin tonight with the launch of an
electronic system called MarketXT. The 6 p.m. to 8 p.m. Eastern-time session is a step toward
round-the-clock trading.
26
Cisco agrees to buy Cerent, a closely held networking company, for about $6.9 billion in stock. The purchase,
Cisco's costliest to date, is another sign of the impact of the Internet on corporate valuations.
Asarco and Cyprus Amax sweeten the terms of their merger to fend off an unsolicited bid of $2.64 billion from
Phelps Dodge to acquire the copper concerns. Phelps Dodge doesn't follow up by sweetening the terms of its
stock-swap offers and says that if shareholders approve the merger, Phelps will withdraw its bid.
27
Daewoo's local creditors place 12 of its affiliates in a debt-restructuring program after approving the
conglomerate's restructuring plan. The restructuring is an important step in South Korea's effort to reform the
economy after its financial crisis.
30
Venezuela's Chavez seizes the upper hand in a confrontation between Congress and a constitutional
assembly he controls. The assembly has usurped most legislative powers and ordered Congress not to
convene. In following days, Congress is stripped of all remaining powers and effectively closed by the
constitutional assembly. The moves in what is viewed as a Chavez power grab have foreign investors scared.
Nasdaq officials will keep some of the market's trade-reporting and stock-quote systems open until 6:30 p.m.
Eastern time, starting Oct. 1.
31
East Timorese defy fears of violence to vote on separating from Indonesia. U.N. officials say more than 90%
of the 430,000 registered voters, and 13,000 people overseas, turned out despite months of intimidation by
pro-Jakarta militias. Many see the large, early turnout as a sign most East Timorese favor independence.
Philip Morris raises prices on all of its major cigarette brands by 18 cents a pack, and other tobacco
companies immediately follow its lead.
Carrefour's merger with Promodes, a $16.34 billion deal, will strengthen the French chain's lead on Wal-Mart
in the race to become the world's most global retailer.

SEPTEMBER
1
Air Canada adopts a poison-pill antitakeover plan in a bid to stall Onex's unsolicited proposal to merge the
carrier with Canadian Airlines.
2
Republic New York's securities unit is being investigated by U.S. prosecutors and regulators for allegedly
inflating the net asset value of an investment fund in which Japanese investors may have placed up to $1
billion, people familiar with the matter say.
3
The board of the New York Stock Exchange votes to proceed with plans for a public offering but delays the
target date until next year.
7
Martin Frankel is captured in Hamburg, Germany, ending an international manhunt. Acting on a tip passed on
by the FBI, police also seize cash and diamonds. He later is indicted on 36 counts of fraud, money
laundering, racketeering and conspiracy. The financier was accused of stealing more than $200 million from
insurance companies in the U.S.
8
A powerful earthquake rocks Athens, killing at least 30 people and leaving more than 100 missing. Most of
the damage from the quake, which had a magnitude of 5.9, is concentrated in working-class and immigrant
areas north of the Greek capital.
Viacom agrees to acquire CBS for about $36 billion in stock in the biggest media deal to date. The question
remains whether the new Viacom, with its expected $21 billion in revenue, will be big enough for both Viacom
Chairman Sumner Redstone, who will be CEO, and CBS Chief Executive Mel Karmazin, who will take over
later.
Hilton reaches an accord to buy Promus Hotel for about $4 billion in cash and stock. The deal represents
something of a comeback for Hilton's CEO, Stephen Bollenbach.
10
Japan intervenes to stem the yen's surge against the dollar. After Tokyo's action, the dollar touches 110 yen
but later recedes slightly. The dollar falls as low as 107.55 yen.
14
An electronic-trading system, Datek's Island unit, plans to buy and sell stocks as late as 8 p.m. Eastern time.
Separately, two investment dealers are taking stakes in Primex Trading, another electronic-trading system.
16
Heinz's talks with Bestfoods, a transaction that would have created the second-biggest food company in the
nation, break down after months of discussions, people familiar with the matter say.
17
A bomb in Russia kills at least 17 in Volgodonsk, bringing the death toll in five recent attacks to 275 and
triggering fears of a political crisis. An explosion in St. Petersburg kills two, but police aren't sure it was a
bomb.
Congress approves a $28.2 billion Treasury bill that doubles the pay of the next president and opens the way
for a $4,600 increase for lawmakers.
20
The Chicago Cubs' Sammy Sosa hits his 61st home run, in a game against Milwaukee. He becomes the first
major leaguer to hit 60 in two different seasons.
21

--- Page 270 ---
Page 270 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
Taiwan is struck by a magnitude-7.6 quake 90 miles southwest of Taipei. Authorities say at least 400 died
when the quake hit. Severe damage is reported in Puli, near the epicenter.
Banque Nationale de Paris plans to launch an all-share offer, valued at about $6.67 billion, to buy out the
35% of Paribas it doesn't already own.
Died: Raisa Gorbachev, 67, wife of the last Soviet president, who added dash and glamour to the glasnost
era, in Muenster, Germany, after battling leukemia.
23
Tobacco companies are hit with a massive lawsuit filed by the Justice Department. It charges the industry
with waging a campaign of deception about the risks of cigarettes, which contribute to the U.S.'s spending
more than $20 billion a year to treat ill smokers.
24
The Dow Jones industrials fall 205.48 to 10318.59, the second 200-point drop this week. Investors jumped to
bonds after Microsoft's Steve Ballmer called prices for tech stocks absurd. The Nasdaq Composite Index
suffers its fourth-worst point decline to date.
27
Asarco's largest shareholder, Grupo Mexico, makes a bid for Asarco that values it at $1.03 billion and alters
the copper-industry takeover battle.
28
U.S. stock exchanges agree to keep the pricing systems for shares listed on the Big Board open until 6:35
p.m. Eastern time. The move effectively extends trading by one to two hours.
OCTOBER
1
Japan fights an uncontrolled nuclear reaction, which has been contained. Three workers are badly hurt as
radiation soars at a plant run by a Sumitomo unit 70 miles northeast of Tokyo. Some 34 others are
contaminated and 310,000 people are warned to stay in their homes. Radiation levels fall after cooling water
is drained, apparently halting fission.
A magnitude-7.5 quake hits Mexico, and early reports say at least 10 people are killed and damage is
extensive in Oaxaca state, 280 miles south of Mexico City.
Phelps Dodge agrees to buy Cyprus Amax for $1.79 billion, snaring one of the two rival copper producers it
has been fighting to acquire. At the same time, Phelps signals it will persist in its hostile struggle for Asarco,
continuing a battle with rival suitor Grupo Mexico.
Ecuador defaults on its Brady bonds, the first nation to do so, as the grace period expires on a $44.5 million
interest payment that was due.
5
MCI WorldCom agrees to buy Sprint for $115 billion in the largest takeover in history. Sprint Chairman and
CEO Esrey is expected to be chairman of the combined company, which would have revenue of over $65
billion and 30% of the consumer long-distance market.
6
Initial indictments are handed up in the Russian money-laundering case. A former Bank of New York vice
president, her husband and a Russian business associate are accused of a conspiracy to transmit about $7
billion illegally. Charges fall short of federal money-laundering offenses, showing the difficulty of sorting out
whether the money was obtained illegally.
7
Phelps Dodge agrees to acquire Asarco for $1.11 billion. But some analysts question if Phelps is paying too
high a price for the copper producer.
8

--- Page 271 ---
Page 271 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
American Home agrees to pay as much as $3.75 billion to settle
lawsuits over its Redux and Pondimin diet drugs in what would be a
record injury settlement involving a pharmaceuticals concern. The
company also says it is adopting a stockholder-rights plan to protect
itself against hostile takeover tactics.
13
Stocks tumble on worries about inflation. The industrials fall 231.12, or 2.17%, to 10417.06, the
second-biggest drop of the year in point terms and fourth-heaviest in percentage terms.
Pakistan's military overthrows the government of the new nuclear power. Troops seize state-run media and
confine Prime Minister Sharif to his home. The army chief accuses him of "systematically destroying" state
institutions and driving the economy toward collapse.
14
Senate Republicans reject the nuclear test-ban treaty in a 51-48 vote. Four Republicans break ranks and
Democrat Byrd abstains, leaving the treaty 19 votes short of ratification. No major treaty has gone down to
defeat since Versailles in 1920.
18
A sharp jump in wholesale prices in September sets off fears on Wall Street that inflation has awakened, but
economists say the numbers are artificially boosted by several one-time factors, and widespread evidence of
rising prices is still slight. Stocks sink 266.90 points to 10019.71, the heaviest drop in percentage terms since
Oct. 1 of last year.
21
Mannesmann agrees to acquire Orange PLC, Britain's third-largest mobile-phone operator, in a $32.93 billion
cash-and-stock deal.
Elizabeth Dole withdraws from the race for the Republican presidential nomination, saying she lacks money
to compete.
22
IBM shares tumble $16, or 15%, in NYSE composite trading, costing the firm $29 billion in market value. The
broad market, though, largely shrugs off IBM's earnings warning.
25
House and Senate conferees reach an agreement with the White House on compromise legislation to
eliminate restrictions in the Glass-Steagall financial-services law that have prohibited banking and securities
firms from fully entering each other's businesses.
26
A Learjet accident kills two-time U.S. Open champion Payne Stewart, 42, two agents, two pilots and a sixth
person when the plane falls nose-first in a field near Mina, S.D., after a flight from Orlando, Fla. The
destination was Dallas; safety analysts suspect a depressurization incapacitated all aboard.
Patrick Buchanan bolts the GOP to seek the Reform Party presidential nomination. He faces a challenge from
casino and real-estate tycoon Donald Trump. Minnesota Gov. Jesse Ventura and party founder Ross Perot
also are viewed as possible contenders.
27
Citigroup announces that Robert Rubin will join the nation's largest financial-services concern. The former
Treasury secretary will serve as chairman of the board's executive committee and as a member of the office
of the chairman with both John Reed and Sanford Weill.
The Dow Jones industrials will undergo one of the biggest overhauls in history, with Microsoft, Intel, SBC and
Home Depot replacing Chevron, Goodyear, Sears and Union Carbide on Nov. 1, reflecting technology's
economic importance. For the first time, two Nasdaq stocks join the 103-year-old index.
29

--- Page 272 ---
Page 272 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
The government reports that gross domestic product grew at an annual rate of 4.8% in the third quarter,
much faster than expected, with few signs of inflationary strain. The employment-cost index rose 0.8%.
Greenspan suggests that he needs to see more evidence the economy is slowing to keep the central bank
from raising interest rates. The Dow Jones industrials rise 227.64 to 10622.53.
NOVEMBER
1
An EgyptAir plane crashes off Nantucket, killing all 217 aboard. Flight 990 left New York's Kennedy Airport on
a trip to Cairo. The Boeing 767-300 was carrying 18 crew and 199 passengers. Pilot suicide emerges as
investigators' chief theory after flight-data and cockpit-voice recorders suggest that one of the pilots
deliberately disengaged the autopilot and put the plane into a steep dive.
4
The Nasdaq composite closes above 3000 for the first time, propelled by enthusiasm for technology stocks.
Intel, which has been an integral part of Nasdaq's success through the years, rises $2.0625 to $79.50. The
Nasdaq composite now has more than doubled in value since early October of last year.
American Home and Warner-Lambert agree to merge in a transaction valued at $72 billion. The deal puts
pressure on AHP's chairman and comes as the drug industry is particularly ripe for consolidation.
5
Pfizer launches an $80 billion all-stock offer for Warner-Lambert, the biggest hostile bid to date. Pfizer's move
is seen as an attempt to grab the cholesterol drug Lipitor and, by combining the two firms' research
operations, create a giant with a $4 billion R&D budget.
8
Microsoft is found by a federal judge to be a relentless and predatory monopolist, in a harsh rebuke to the
company and Chairman Bill Gates. The finding is being scoured by private and corporate lawyers looking for
an opening to seek monetary damages. The company's shares, however, end down only 1.8% after analysts
predict it will emerge from the dispute without serious damage.
9
Israel and the Palestinians launch talks aimed at achieving a permanent peace accord, and set an ambitious
100-day deadline for crafting the broad outlines of a deal. Huge obstacles must be overcome. Among them
are the fate of Jewish settlements and Palestinian refugees, and Jerusalem's status. Both sides claim it as a
capital.
10
The Senate approves a rise in the minimum wage, but tax cuts may sink it. The GOP-crafted plan for a $1
raise over three years, which passes largely on party lines, is paired with $18.4 billion in cuts Clinton vows to
veto as a "cynical" break for special interests. Meanwhile, Republicans agree to add almost $2 billion for
education, the environment and the U.N.
15
Mannesmann rejects an all-stock acquisition proposal from Vodafone AirTouch valuing the German company
at $107.19 billion. Mannesmann says the offer, one of the biggest takeover proposals in history, substantially
undervalues it and wouldn't be a good strategic fit.
16
The U.S. and China sign a landmark deal that could make China a member of the WTO by spring. The broad
agreement, which cuts certain tariffs and liberalizes foreign involvement in Chinese businesses, still requires
U.S. congressional approval.
Vodafone AirTouch weighs a hostile takeover of Mannesmann after the German company spurned its
acquisition proposal.
17

--- Page 273 ---
Page 273 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
The Fed raises interest rates for the third time this year, but suggests it will pause in its aggressive
campaign to rein in the U.S. economy. The central bank says it is confident the quarter-percentage-point
increase should accomplish its chief objective of "markedly" diminishing "the risk of inflation going forward."
19
Twelve college students die when a 40-foot log pyramid built for a Texas A&M bonfire collapses on them.
23
Iraq stops oil exports, signaling an escalating battle over U.N. sanctions. Baghdad had rejected extending a
U.N. program under which it is allowed limited oil sales to pay for civilian goods. The oil cutoff is unexpected,
however, and occurs during a period of rising international demand. For Saddam Hussein, the move shows
his intention to fight a U.N. bid to revive arms inspections in return for relaxing the sanctions. Oil futures rise
on the news, reaching a post-Gulf War high of $27.15 a barrel during the trading day.
24
Pfizer sues Warner-Lambert, claiming the company violated a provision of their pact to jointly market Lipitor,
and asks a Delaware state court to stop the merger of Warner-Lambert and American Home Products. The
suit, which also names AHP as a defendant, comes as Warner-Lambert's board mulls taking legal action
against Pfizer.
28
The euro's plunge to a historic low of $1.0155, along with the rise in the yen, to 101.72 to the dollar, puts
strong pressure on the U.S., European and Japanese governments to restore stability in the global currency
markets.
DECEMBER
1
Protesters disrupt the first day of the World Trade Organization's Seattle conference. A curfew is imposed
and the National Guard is called in as police fight assorted foes of global capitalism. Poor nations' delegates
threaten to block a new round of trade talks.
2
Carnival announces a hostile $1.7 billion takeover bid for the parent of Norwegian Cruise Lines, NCL Holding,
which is urging its holders not to accept the offer. NCL ADRs rise 30%.
Large stocks rally, led by technology and Internet shares. The Dow Jones industrials climb 120.58 points to
10998.39. The Nasdaq composite rises for the first time in three sessions and the dollar strengthens.
McDonald's agrees to buy Boston Chicken, operator of the Boston Market chain of restaurants, for $173.5
million.
Britain hands over significant power to the new Protestant-Catholic government in Northern Ireland in a
historic step toward ending decades of sectarian warfare in the province.
3
The euro touches parity with the dollar for the first time, declining 15% since its historic launch Jan. 1 as
Europe's common currency. The euro trades below $1 before strengthening to $1.0019 late in New York, but
the fall below the psychologically important parity level reflects concerns that European economies aren't
matching the robust expansion of the U.S. European Central Bank President Wim Duisenberg says
Germany's recent behavior has hurt the euro.
The Nasdaq composite soars nearly 3% to a record 3452.78, reflecting investors' zeal for technology issues.
The Dow Jones Industrial Average rises 40.67 points to 11039.06.
6
AT&T will announce plans for an IPO of up to 20% of its wireless operations, people close to the situation
say. The offering will be the nation's largest to date, generating $8 billion to $10 billion for the phone
company, and will mark the first time AT&T has significantly changed its structure since the Lucent spinoff in
1995.

--- Page 274 ---
Page 274 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
NASA scientists' hopes dwindle as an attempt to contact the Mars Polar Lander through a Mars orbiter fails,
increasing fears that the craft may have been lost during landing.
Six firefighters die in an abandoned-warehouse fire in Worcester, Mass. Two entered to look for trapped
homeless people and ran into trouble. Four others then attempted a rescue.
7
A ValuJet ex-contractor is convicted on nine felony charges tied to
mishandling of oxygen generators blamed in the 1996 crash that killed
110. Two employees are acquitted. SabreTech, a now-defunct Sabreliner
unit, faces fines of up to $4.5 million and restitution to victims.
Edmond Safra's nurse confesses to setting the fire that killed the
financier and a second nurse Friday, prosecutors in Monaco say.
American Ted Maher, 41, apparently was trying to fake an attack by
intruders in a bid to impress Safra.
Coca-Cola Chairman M. Douglas Ivester, who was the handpicked successor of the late Roberto Goizueta,
steps down, shocking colleagues and the business community. He will retire in April and stay on as a
consultant for a number of years. He recommends that Douglas Daft, head of Coke's businesses in the
Middle and Far East and Africa, succeed him.
9
Martin Luther King was killed as part of a conspiracy, not an assassin operating on his own, a Tennessee civil
jury decides. The finding comes in a case in which the King family sued a retired Memphis businessman who
has said he paid someone other than James Earl Ray to kill King.
10
VA Linux rockets 698% to $239.25, the biggest opening-day gain to date for an IPO in the U.S. It is the first
time an offering ends the regular session above $200 on the Nasdaq Stock Market. The Nasdaq sees over
1.7 billion shares change hands, a record.
14
AMR is expected to announce plans for a $6.2 billion spinoff of Sabre Holdings and the hiring of a
telecommunications executive to head the newly independent computer-services firm, people familiar with the
moves say. The spinoff will split the parent of American Airlines in half and free Sabre to deal in technology
outsourcing and Internet-based travel sales. Shares of AMR and Sabre rise.
Died: Joseph Heller, 76, author best known for his darkly comic World War II novel, "Catch-22," at his home
in East Hampton, N.Y., of a heart attack.
15
Viacom's MTV Networks is under investigation by the Justice Department for alleged antitrust violations in
dealings with major music companies, according to federal officials.
A New York state judge issues orders prohibiting New York City's bus and subway workers from staging a
crippling strike as talks continue. A walkout would affect 3.5 million commuters.
16
Major music companies have talked with federal antitrust enforcers about settling allegations that they acted
illegally to discourage retail discounting of compact disks, industry lawyers say. The FTC investigation marks
a second antitrust probe of music-industry practices and apparently has delayed the agency's approval of the
CDNow-Columbia House merger.
Exxon Mobil plans to cut its work force by 12%, or 14,000 employees, and gain $3.8 billion in annual pretax
savings, far more than original figures suggested.
17
Pharmacia and Monsanto are in merger discussions, people familiar with the matter say, but a deal is far from
ensured and is just one option Monsanto's board is considering as a means of boosting shareholder value.
Monsanto has a market capitalization of about $26 billion; Pharmacia is valued at $28 billion.

--- Page 275 ---
Page 275 of 277 © 2025 Factiva, Inc. All rights reserved.
Star Cruises increases its stake in NCL to 51%, effectively gaining control of Norwegian Cruise Line's parent.
Carnival drops its bid for NCL.
20
Burlington Northern Santa Fe and Canadian National Railway agree to combine their rail systems, creating
North America's largest railroad, according to people familiar with the transaction. The merger would be
valued at about $6 billion, plus the assumption of long-term debt. The combined entity would have revenue of
$12.5 billion.
Pharmacia and Monsanto's boards approve a $27 billion merger of equals to transform the two midtier
pharmaceutical concerns into a formidable competitor in the drug industry.
21
The flood toll in Venezuela continues to climb, with officials estimating the number of dead from 5,000 to
30,000 and the number of evacuees from 40,000 to 100,000. Desperate survivors skirmish with police in La
Guaira as they try to seize food. The Internet is being used to try to account for many still missing.
30
The Nasdaq composite closes above the 4000 milestone, at 4041.46, up 84% on the year. It is the star in a
day of stock-market records. The Dow Jones industrials add 0.07% to 11484.66, and the S&P 500 gains 5.80
points to 1463.46. The Russell 2000 index of small-cap stocks climbs to 497.01, up 8.53 points.
31
Russian President Boris Yeltsin, 68, announces he is resigning earlier than planned because Russia should
enter the new millennium with new leaders. He says he is quitting because of poor health and many other
reasons. He appoints Prime Minister Vladimir Putin as acting president.
More than 150 passengers are freed after eight days aboard an Indian Airlines plane hijacked to Afghanistan,
after their captors forge a deal with the Indian government to win the release of three jailed militants. The
Airbus 300 was seized by five men after leaving Nepal and made brief stops in India, Pakistan and the United
Arab Emirates, where 27 hostages were freed. Hijackers killed at least one man
Died: Sarah Knauss, 119, the world's oldest person, in Allentown, Pa.
